The user wants A LOT of agents running concurrently.\n\n**Direction C covers building the full CSS cascade — the key differentiator vs jsdom (which never achieved this). Built on Servo's `cssparser` and `selectors` crates.**\n\n**Components to plan:**\n\n1. **CSS parsing** — Use `cssparser` to tokenize and parse CSS stylesheets into a structured representation (list of rules, each with a selector list and declaration block)\n2. **Selector matching** — Implement the `selectors::Element` trait on our DomTree nodes so we can use the `selectors` crate to match CSS selectors against elements. This is also a prerequisite for querySelector/querySelectorAll in Direction B.\n3. **Stylesheet collection** — Collect all `<style>` elements and inline `style=\"\"` attributes from the parsed DOM. Later: external `<link rel=\"stylesheet\">` loading.\n4. **Cascade algorithm** — For each element, collect all matching rules, sort by specificity + source order + importance, produce the \"cascaded value\" for each property\n5. **CSS property system** — Define the set of CSS properties we support, their initial values, whether they inherit, and how to compute them (e.g., `em` → `px`, `inherit` → parent's value, percentages)\n6. **Computed style** — For each element, resolve cascaded values through inheritance and initial values to produce final computed styles\n7. **getComputedStyle()** — JS binding that returns a CSSStyleDeclaration-like object for any element\n8. **element.style** — JS binding for inline style read/write (CSSStyleDeclaration)\n9. **display:none handling** — Elements with `display:none` should be excluded from the a11y tree\n10. **visibility:hidden handling** — Elements with `visibility:hidden` should have their text excluded but structure preserved\n\n**Key Servo crate APIs to understand:**\n- `cssparser::Parser` — tokenizes and parses CSS\n- `cssparser::DeclarationParser`, `RuleBodyParser`, `QualifiedRuleParser` — traits you implement to handle parsed CSS constructs\n- `selectors::SelectorImpl` — trait to define your selector types\n- `selectors::Element` — trait you implement on your DOM element type to enable selector matching\n- `selectors::matching::matches_selector()` — the core matching function\n\n**New dependencies needed in engine/Cargo.toml:**\n```toml\ncssparser = \"0.34\"\nselectors = \"0.28\"\n```\n(Verify these are the latest versions compatible with each other — they're both from Servo.)\n\n**Design the plan as waves of parallel agents.** The CSS pipeline has a natural dependency chain (parse → match → cascade → compute → bind to JS), but within each stage there are parallelizable pieces.\n\n**For each agent task, specify:**\n- What files it creates/edits\n- What it implements (be specific about traits and their methods)\n- What tests it should write\n- What it depends on (which prior wave/agent)\n\n**Output format:** A clear wave-by-wave plan with agent descriptions, dependencies, and test expectations. {"parentUuid":"63bb393f-46eb-41c6-a5c7-1c2ba7ec284e","isSidechain":true,"userType":"external","cwd":"/Users/danielkim/sandbox/tools/text-browser","sessionId":"dd951cf3-4bdc-4767-b581-34b4ad2c2cfe","version":"2.1.34","gitBranch":"HEAD","agentId":"aa84c6d","slug":"tingly-leaping-muffin","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_019ho8qTXCs5g9pvXPxK2bhT","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→# Braille\n     2→\n     3→A lightweight browser that maintains a virtual DOM with full JavaScript execution but skips graphical rendering entirely. Outputs structured text representations of pages for LLM agents to read and interact with.\n     4→\n     5→A browser for those who read, not see.\n     6→\n     7→**Spike:** [SPIKE.md](./SPIKE.md) — COMPLETE (46 tests, core loop proven)\n     8→**API Reference:** [REFERENCE.md](./REFERENCE.md) — Boa and html5ever API details\n     9→\n    10→## Status\n    11→\n    12→Spike complete. The core loop works: HTML in → html5ever parse → DomTree → Boa JS execution → DOM mutation → a11y text snapshot out. CLI can `braille <sid> goto <url>` to fetch a page, execute inline scripts, and print an accessibility tree.\n    13→\n    14→### What exists (46 tests)\n    15→\n    16→| Component | Status | What works |\n    17→|-----------|--------|------------|\n    18→| DOM tree | Arena-based, basic ops | createElement, appendChild, removeChild, getElementById, getElementsByTagName, textContent get/set |\n    19→| HTML parser | html5ever TreeSink | Full spec-compliant HTML parsing into DomTree |\n    20→| JS engine | Boa bindings | `document.createElement`, `document.getElementById`, `element.textContent`, `element.appendChild` |\n    21→| A11y serializer | Basic roles | headings, paragraphs, links, buttons, inputs, lists, images, nav, main, form; interactive refs (@e1) |\n    22→| Wire protocol | serde types | Command/Response/SnapMode enums |\n    23→| CLI | clap arg parsing | `new`, `goto` (live fetch + render), `click`/`type`/`snap`/`back`/`forward`/`close` (stubs) |\n    24→| Engine | Integration | `load_html` (parse + execute scripts), `snapshot` (a11y mode) |\n    25→\n    26→### What doesn't exist yet\n    27→\n    28→| Component | Gap |\n    29→|-----------|-----|\n    30→| Session state | No persistence between CLI commands — each `goto` creates a new Engine |\n    31→| DOM API surface | Only 4 methods. Real sites need 50+: querySelector, innerHTML, setAttribute, classList, parentNode, addEventListener, etc. |\n    32→| CSS cascade | Not started. cssparser + selectors integration, specificity, inheritance, computed values, getComputedStyle() |\n    33→| Layout | Not started. Taffy integration, getBoundingClientRect, offsetWidth/Height |\n    34→| Event system | No event dispatch — click/type commands are stubs |\n    35→| External resources | No `<script src=\"...\">`, no CSS file loading, no relative URL resolution |\n    36→| Navigation | No history, no cookie jar, no redirects, no SPA routing |\n    37→| WASM sandbox | Not started — engine runs in-process |\n    38→\n    39→## What's Next\n    40→\n    41→Three possible directions, in order of impact:\n    42→\n    43→### Direction A: Make it actually usable (session + interaction)\n    44→Make `braille` a working tool an agent can use end-to-end: persistent sessions, click/type work, external script loading.\n    45→- Session manager (in-process HashMap of session ID → Engine)\n    46→- Event dispatch (click fires click event, type fills input value)\n    47→- External `<script src>` fetching\n    48→- Cookie jar per session\n    49→\n    50→### Direction B: DOM API surface (framework compatibility)\n    51→Expand the DOM API until real sites work. Start with static sites, work toward SPAs.\n    52→- querySelector/querySelectorAll (needs CSS selector matching)\n    53→- innerHTML/outerHTML (parse + serialize)\n    54→- setAttribute/getAttribute/removeAttribute\n    55→- classList (add/remove/toggle/contains)\n    56→- parentNode, children, nextSibling, previousSibling\n    57→- addEventListener/removeEventListener + event propagation\n    58→- window.location, window.setTimeout (stub)\n    59→\n    60→### Direction C: CSS cascade\n    61→Build the differentiating feature — full CSS cascade that jsdom never achieved.\n    62→- cssparser integration for stylesheet parsing\n    63→- selectors crate for selector matching\n    64→- Cascade algorithm (specificity, source order, importance)\n    65→- Inheritance and initial values\n    66→- getComputedStyle()\n    67→- display:none → skip in a11y output\n    68→\n    69→These are not mutually exclusive — Direction B is the highest-volume work and can be parallelized heavily.\n    70→\n    71→## Core Thesis\n    72→\n    73→LLMs don't need pixels — they need text. The DOM is already a text structure. The graphical rendering pipeline (layout, paint, compositing, GPU) is the expensive part of a browser, and agents don't need any of it. An LLM can look at raw DOM with inline styles and understand the visual intent: `display: none` means hidden, `position: fixed; top: 0` means sticky header.\n    74→\n    75→## Requirements\n    76→\n    77→- Full JavaScript execution against a live DOM\n    78→- Agents can navigate, click links, fill forms, follow redirects\n    79→- Handles modern SPA frameworks (React, SvelteKit at minimum)\n    80→- CSS changes from JS are reflected in the DOM text output\n    81→- Lightweight — the whole point is avoiding headless Chrome overhead\n    82→- Structured text output designed for LLM consumption\n    83→- WASM sandboxing — untrusted page JS executes inside a sandboxed module\n    84→- Distributed as a single CLI binary agents can `brew install`\n    85→\n    86→## Stack\n    87→\n    88→### Language: Rust\n    89→- Entire engine written in Rust — DOM, CSS cascade, layout, all in one codebase\n    90→- Compiles to native binary for CLI distribution\n    91→- The engine compiles to WASM for sandboxed execution of untrusted page JS\n    92→- No FFI boundaries within the engine — DOM and JS engine are both Rust, same memory model\n    93→- Single binary output, no runtime dependencies\n    94→\n    95→### JS Engine: Boa\n    96→- Pure Rust JavaScript engine — no C dependencies, no language bridging\n    97→- 94.12% Test262 conformance (v0.21), actively improving\n    98→- Embeds directly into the Rust codebase — DOM calls from page JS are just Rust function calls, no FFI overhead\n    99→- Compiles to WASM natively alongside the DOM implementation\n   100→- Risk: younger than V8/JSC/QuickJS, may hit spec gaps on real-world sites. Mitigated by active development and our ability to contribute upstream.\n   101→\n   102→### Servo Crates (dependencies)\n   103→\n   104→| Crate | Purpose | License |\n   105→|-------|---------|---------|\n   106→| **html5ever** | HTML parsing, spec-compliant, passes html5lib-tests | MIT/Apache-2.0 |\n   107→| **cssparser** | CSS tokenization and parsing (CSS Syntax Level 3) | MPL-2.0 |\n   108→| **selectors** | CSS selector parsing and matching against DOM elements | MPL-2.0 |\n   109→| **taffy** | Layout computation — CSS Block, Flexbox, and Grid | MIT/Apache-2.0 |\n   110→\n   111→### Custom Implementation (what we build)\n   112→- **DOM** — Rust implementation from scratch, spec-compliant, validated against WPT\n   113→- **CSS Cascade Engine** — specificity, cascade ordering, inheritance, computed values. Built on top of `cssparser` + `selectors`.\n   114→- **`getComputedStyle()`** — full spec compliance. React and other frameworks depend on this.\n   115→- **Accessibility tree generator** — transforms live DOM into compact text representation for agents\n   116→- **Session manager** — stateful sessions with cookies, history, navigation\n   117→- **CLI interface** — the `braille` command\n   118→- **Event loop** — frozen time model with pump-to-settled semantics\n   119→\n   120→### Project Structure\n   121→\n   122→Cargo workspace with 3 crates, separated by the WASM compilation boundary:\n   123→\n   124→```\n   125→braille/\n   126→├── Cargo.toml                  # workspace root\n   127→├── PLAN.md\n   128→├── crates/\n   129→│   ├── engine/                 # compiles to WASM — the sandboxed browser\n   130→│   │   ├── Cargo.toml\n   131→│   │   └── src/\n   132→│   │       ├── lib.rs\n   133→│   │       ├── dom/            # Node, Element, Document, Event, etc.\n   134→│   │       ├── css/            # cascade, specificity, computed styles\n   135→│   │       ├── layout/         # Taffy integration\n   136→│   │       ├── html/           # html5ever integration\n   137→│   │       ├── js/             # Boa integration, Web API bindings\n   138→│   │       ├── a11y/           # accessibility tree generation\n   139→│   │       └── event_loop/     # frozen time pump-to-settled loop\n   140→│   │\n   141→│   ├── wire/                   # shared types — the WASM boundary contract\n   142→│   │   ├── Cargo.toml\n   143→│   │   └── src/\n   144→│   │       └── lib.rs          # commands, responses, snapshot formats, element refs\n   145→│   │\n   146→│   └── cli/                    # native binary — the host\n   147→│       ├── Cargo.toml\n   148→│       └── src/\n   149→│           ├── main.rs\n   150→│           ├── session.rs      # session lifecycle, ID management\n   151→│           └── network.rs      # reqwest, cookie jar, fetch proxying\n   152→│\n   153→└── tests/\n   154→    ├── wpt/                    # WPT test harness\n   155→    ├── html5lib/               # html5lib-tests harness\n   156→    └── fixtures/               # reference HTML pages for integration tests\n   157→```\n   158→\n   159→**`engine`** — Everything that runs inside the WASM sandbox. Zero I/O, zero networking, pure computation. Takes parsed HTML + fetched resources as input, produces snapshots as output. Hard rule: if it touches the outside world, it doesn't go here.\n   160→\n   161→**`wire`** — The protocol between engine and CLI. Command types (`Goto`, `Click`, `Type`), response types (`Snapshot`, `Error`), element reference formats (`@button3`), snapshot mode enums. Both `engine` and `cli` depend on this. Forces the WASM boundary to be explicit and well-defined.\n   162→\n   163→**`cli`** — The native host. Loads the engine, provides networking on behalf of the sandbox (engine requests a URL → CLI fetches it → passes the response back in), manages sessions, parses CLI args, formats output.\n   164→\n   165→## Form Factor: CLI (`braille`)\n   166→\n   167→Single native binary, distributed via `brew install`, `cargo install`, or direct download.\n   168→No SDK to import, no server to start, no runtime dependencies.\n   169→Cross-platform: macOS, Linux, Windows.\n   170→\n   171→### Session-based interface\n   172→```\n   173→braille new                              # → returns session ID\n   174→braille <sid> goto <url>                 # navigate, returns snapshot\n   175→braille <sid> click <selector>           # click element, returns snapshot\n   176→braille <sid> type <selector> \"text\"     # fill input, returns snapshot\n   177→braille <sid> select <selector> \"value\"  # select dropdown, returns snapshot\n   178→braille <sid> focus <selector>           # focus element\n   179→braille <sid> snap                       # get current snapshot\n   180→braille <sid> snap --mode=markdown       # snapshot in specific mode\n   181→braille <sid> back                       # go back\n   182→braille <sid> forward                    # go forward\n   183→braille <sid> close                      # end session\n   184→```\n   185→\n   186→Every mutation command returns a snapshot automatically.\n   187→Verbs mirror what a human does in a browser.\n   188→\n   189→## Agent Interface\n   190→\n   191→Agent chooses output mode based on use case:\n   192→- **Accessibility tree (default)** — compact, semantic, ~200-400 tokens. Interactive elements get stable references (e.g. `@button3`, `@input7`)\n   193→- **Simplified DOM** — strips noise (scripts, hidden elements, SVG internals, empty wrappers), keeps meaningful structure with interactive markers\n   194→- **Raw DOM** — full HTML serialization for debugging or when the agent needs everything\n   195→- **Markdown** — readable content extraction for articles, docs, etc.\n   196→\n   197→Agent interacts via element references: `click @button3`, `type @input7 \"search query\"`, `select @dropdown2 \"option1\"`\n   198→\n   199→Must support: clicking links/buttons, filling form inputs, selecting dropdowns, submitting forms, scrolling.\n   200→\n   201→## CSS: Full Spec Compliance\n   202→\n   203→- Full CSS cascade: parsing, selector matching, specificity, inheritance, computed values\n   204→- `getComputedStyle()` must work correctly\n   205→- Built on Servo's `cssparser` (parsing) and `selectors` (matching) crates\n   206→- Cascade algorithm, inheritance, initial values, shorthand expansion — custom implementation on top of those crates\n   207→- This is a significant differentiator — jsdom never solved this (open PR from 2019, never merged)\n   208→- WPT has CSS tests to validate against\n   209→\n   210→## Layout: Taffy\n   211→\n   212→- **Taffy** provides real CSS Block, Flexbox, and Grid layout computation\n   213→- Input: tree of nodes with CSS Style structs → Output: Layout structs with position (x, y) and size (width, height)\n   214→- This gives us correct `getBoundingClientRect()`, `offsetWidth`, `offsetHeight` values\n   215→- Viewport is configurable, defaults to 1280x720, agent can change it\n   216→- Text measurement approximated (char count × avg char width × font size) — no font renderer\n   217→- Skips: subpixel rendering, paint order, z-index stacking contexts\n   218→\n   219→## Navigation: Stateful Sessions\n   220→\n   221→- Browser interaction is through stateful sessions. Agent gets a session ID, issues commands against it.\n   222→- Session owns: DOM, cookies, history, navigation context\n   223→- Full page navigation: teardown current DOM, fetch new page, parse and rebuild\n   224→- SPA routing: `pushState`/`replaceState`/`popstate` handled naturally by executing the page's JS\n   225→- Back/forward history: supported\n   226→- Iframes: supported — each iframe gets its own document within the parent session\n   227→\n   228→## Network\n   229→\n   230→- **Rust HTTP client** (reqwest or similar) for HTTP requests\n   231→- **Cookie jar per session** — persists across navigations, attaches correct cookies to outgoing requests\n   232→- **CORS: skip by default** — no user to protect, agent wants cross-origin access. Optionally enforceable.\n   233→- **Service workers: supported** — needed for sites that rely on them for request interception/routing\n   234→\n   235→## Security: WASM Sandboxing\n   236→\n   237→- Page JS executes inside a WASM sandbox — even memory exploits can't escape\n   238→- The entire engine (Rust DOM + Boa JS) compiles to a WASM module\n   239→- The host (native CLI binary) only provides controlled capabilities: network access, session management\n   240→- No file system access, no process spawning from within the sandbox\n   241→\n   242→## Execution Model: Frozen Time\n   243→\n   244→- Time freezes between agent commands. No JS runs until the agent acts.\n   245→- On each command (goto, click, type, etc.):\n   246→  1. Execute the action\n   247→  2. Pump the event loop — process microtasks, fire ready timers, handle network callbacks\n   248→  3. Keep pumping until \"settled\" (no pending microtasks, no ready timers, network quiet)\n   249→  4. Freeze. Return snapshot.\n   250→- `setTimeout(fn, 5000)` doesn't fire on wall clock — it fires when the event loop is pumped past that point\n   251→- Every mutation command returns a snapshot automatically. `snap` is for looking without acting.\n   252→- More deterministic than a real browser — no race conditions, agent always sees consistent state\n   253→\n   254→### Needs deeper design work:\n   255→- **Web Workers** — separate threads in real browsers. Same event loop? Separate WASM instances? Freeze between commands?\n   256→- **Async/await and Promises** — microtask queue should pump naturally during \"settle\", but edge cases need verification\n   257→- **Streams** — ReadableStream, WritableStream, fetch body streams. Behavior when time is frozen?\n   258→- **WebSockets** — persistent connections. Messages queue up and deliver on next pump?\n   259→- **requestAnimationFrame** — no screen to paint, but frameworks use it for scheduling. Treat as a timer?\n   260→\n   261→## Compliance Testing\n   262→\n   263→- **WPT (Web Platform Tests)** — 56,000+ test files, BSD licensed, the canonical browser conformance suite\n   264→  - jsdom's `to-run.yaml` provides a curated roadmap of which tests are feasible for non-browser DOM implementations\n   265→  - Start with `dom/nodes/`, `dom/events/`, `html/dom/`, `css/selectors/`\n   266→- **html5lib-tests** — 9,200+ HTML parser test cases, MIT licensed\n   267→  - Validates that HTML parsing produces correct DOM trees\n   268→- **Test262** — Boa already runs this; monitor their conformance progress\n   269→\n   270→## Licensing\n   271→\n   272→- Braille: MIT or Apache-2.0\n   273→- Boa: MIT — compatible\n   274→- Servo crates: MPL-2.0 (cssparser, selectors) and MIT/Apache-2.0 (html5ever, taffy) — all compatible\n   275→- AGPL is a dealbreaker (ruled out Lightpanda)\n   276→\n   277→## Landscape: What Exists and Why It's Not Enough\n   278→\n   279→### Agent browser tools (full Chrome underneath)\n   280→- **agent-browser** (Vercel Labs) — great text output via accessibility trees, but Playwright/headless Chrome under the hood\n   281→- **browser-use** — LLM-driven browser automation, still Playwright\n   282→- **Stagehand** (Browserbase) — same, real Chromium\n   283→- **Playwright MCP** (Microsoft) — accessibility tree for LLMs, still a full browser\n   284→\n   285→These solve the output format problem but not the rendering overhead problem.\n   286→\n   287→### Virtual DOMs (no real JS execution)\n   288→- **jsdom** — most complete DOM, but weak in-page JS execution, slow\n   289→- **happy-dom** — faster, but had an RCE vulnerability (CVE-2025-61927), less spec-compliant\n   290→- **linkedom** — minimal, designed for SSR not browser emulation\n   291→\n   292→These are DOM parsers, not browsers.\n   293→\n   294→### Lightpanda\n   295→- Closest to our vision architecturally — Zig-based, V8, real DOM, no rendering\n   296→- But: AGPL licensed (dealbreaker), beta quality, small team, Zig pre-1.0\n   297→- Missing many Web APIs, SPAs don't work reliably\n   298→\n   299→### Content extraction tools (Firecrawl, Jina Reader, Crawl4AI)\n   300→- One-shot extraction, not interactive browsers\n   301→- Still use full browsers internally\n   302→\n   303→## Open Items\n   304→\n   305→### Framework Acceptance Criteria\n   306→- React's reconciler touches a LOT of DOM APIs — need to enumerate which ones\n   307→- SvelteKit compiles to direct DOM manipulation — different API surface\n   308→- Need to identify the minimum DOM API surface that makes these frameworks functional\n   309→- **TODO (later):** Identify real-world reference sites/apps to use as test targets:\n   310→  - Official/canonical framework examples\n   311→  - Real production SPAs\n   312→  - Minimal reproduction apps for specific DOM API surfaces (forms, routing, dynamic content)\n   313→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should     1→use crate::dom::node::{NodeData, NodeId};\n     2→use crate::dom::DomTree;\n     3→\n     4→/// Elements that are completely skipped (not recursed into).\n     5→const SKIP_ELEMENTS: &[&str] = &[\"head\", \"script\", \"style\", \"meta\", \"link\", \"noscript\"];\n     6→\n     7→/// Elements that are transparent containers: they don't produce a role line,\n     8→/// and their children appear at the same indentation level.\n     9→const TRANSPARENT_ELEMENTS: &[&str] = &[\n    10→    \"div\", \"span\", \"section\", \"article\", \"header\", \"footer\", \"html\", \"body\",\n    11→];\n    12→\n    13→/// Elements that receive interactive `@eN` references.\n    14→const INTERACTIVE_ELEMENTS: &[&str] = &[\"a\", \"button\", \"input\", \"textarea\", \"select\"];\n    15→\n    16→/// Walk a `DomTree` and produce a compact accessibility-tree text\n    17→/// representation suitable for LLM agents.\n    18→pub fn serialize_a11y(tree: &DomTree) -> String {\n    19→    let mut output = String::new();\n    20→    let mut ref_counter: usize = 0;\n    21→    walk(tree, tree.document(), 0, &mut ref_counter, &mut output);\n    22→    // Trim trailing newline for cleaner output\n    23→    while output.ends_with('\\n') {\n    24→        output.pop();\n    25→    }\n    26→    output\n    27→}\n    28→\n    29→fn walk(\n    30→    tree: &DomTree,\n    31→    node_id: NodeId,\n    32→    indent: usize,\n    33→    ref_counter: &mut usize,\n    34→    output: &mut String,\n    35→) {\n    36→    let node = tree.get_node(node_id);\n    37→\n    38→    match &node.data {\n    39→        NodeData::Document => {\n    40→            // Document root: just recurse into children at same indent level.\n    41→            let children: Vec<NodeId> = node.children.clone();\n    42→            for child_id in children {\n    43→                walk(tree, child_id, indent, ref_counter, output);\n    44→            }\n    45→        }\n    46→        NodeData::Text { .. } | NodeData::Comment { .. } => {\n    47→            // Text and Comment nodes are never rendered on their own;\n    48→            // text content is collected by the parent element's role line.\n    49→        }\n    50→        NodeData::Element {\n    51→            tag_name,\n    52→            attributes,\n    53→        } => {\n    54→            let tag = tag_name.to_ascii_lowercase();\n    55→\n    56→            // Skip elements we should never render or recurse into.\n    57→            if SKIP_ELEMENTS.contains(&tag.as_str()) {\n    58→                return;\n    59→            }\n    60→\n    61→            if TRANSPARENT_ELEMENTS.contains(&tag.as_str()) {\n    62→                // Transparent: no role line, recurse at same indent.\n    63→                let children: 67→                return;\n    68→            }\n    69→\n    70→            // This element has a role. Determine the role string.\n    71→            let role = element_role(&tag, attributes);\n    72→\n    73→            // Collect display text: for img elements, use alt attribute;\n    74→            // for all other elements, use immediate Text children.\n    75→            let direct_text = if tag == \"img\" {\n    76→                attributes\n    77→                    .iter()\n    78→                    .find(|(k, _)| k == \"alt\")\n    79→                    .map(|(_, v)| v.clone())\n    80→                    .unwrap_or_default()\n    81→            } else {\n    82→                collect_direct_text(tree, node_id)\n    83→            };\n    84→\n    85→            // Determine if this is an interactive element that needs a ref.\n    86→            let eref = if INTERACTIVE_ELEMENTS.contains(&tag.as_str()) {\n    87→                *ref_counter += 1;\n    88→                Some(format!(\"@e{}\", *ref_counter))\n    89→            } else {\n    90→                None\n    91→            };\n    92→\n    93→            // Check if this element has any interesting children\n    94→            // (non-text element descendants that would produce output).\n    95→            let has_child_output = has_renderable_children(tree, node_id);\n    96→\n    97→            // Skip empty elements: no text and no interesting children.\n    98→            if direct_text.is_empty() && !has_child_output {\n    99→                // Still need a role line if it's interactive (e.g., empty button).\n   100→                // But for non-interactive empty elements, skip entirely.\n   101→                if eref.is_none() {\n   102→                    return;\n   103→                }\n   104→            }\n   105→\n   106→            // Build the role line.\n   107→            let indent_str = \" \".repeat(indent);\n   108→            let mut line = format!(\"{}{}\", indent_str, role);\n   109→\n   110→            if let Some(ref r) = eref {\n   111→                line.push(' ');\n   112→                line.push_str(r);\n   113→            }\n   114→\n   115→            if !direct_text.is_empty() {\n   116→ // Recurse into children at increased indent.\n   123→            let children: Vec<NodeId> = node.children.clone();\n   124→            for child_id in children {\n   125→                walk(tree, child_id, indent + 2, ref_counter, output);\n   126→            }\n   127→        }\n   128→    }\n   129→}\n   130→\n   131→/// Map an element tag to its accessibility role string.\n   132→fn element_role(tag: &str, attributes: &[(String, String)]) -> String {\n   133→    match tag {\n   134→        \"h1\" => \"heading[1]\".to_string(),\n   135→        \"h2\" => \"heading[2]\".to_string(),\n   136→        \"h3\" => \"heading[3]\".to_string(),\n   137→        \"h4\" => \"heading[4]\".to_string(),\n   138→        \"h5\" => \"heading[5]\".to_string(),\n   139→        \"h6\" => \"heading[6]\".to_string(),\n   140→        \"p\" => \"paragraph\".to_string(),\n   141→        \"a\" => \"link\".to_string(),\n   142→        \"button\" => \"button\".to_string(),\n   143→        \"input\" => {\n   144→            if let Some(type_val) = attributes.iter().find(|(k, _)| k == \"type\").map(|(_, v)| v) {\n   145→                format!(\"input[type={}]\", type_val)\n Element QualNames are stored in a parallel Vec so that\n    19→/// `elem_name` can return a borrow from `self` (not from inside the RefCell).\n    20→struct BrailleSink {\n    21→    tree: Rc<RefCell<DomTree>>,\n    22→    names: RefCell<Vec<Option<QualName>>>,\n    23→}\n    24→\n    25→impl BrailleSink {\n    26→    fn new() -> Self {\n    27→        let tree = Rc::new(RefCell::new(DomTree::new()));\n    28→        // Index 0 is the Document root — no QualName for it.\n    29→        let names = RefCell::new(vec![None]);\n    30→        BrailleSink { tree, names }\n    31→    }\n    32→}\n    33→\n    34→impl TreeSink for BrailleSink {\n    35→    type Handle = NodeId;\n    36→    type Output = Rc<RefCell<DomTree>>;\n    37→    type ElemName<'a> = &'a QualName;\n    38→\n    39→    fn finish(self) -> Self::Output {\n    40→        self.tree\n    41→    }\n    42→\n    43→    fn parse_error(&self, _msg: Cow<'static, str>) {\n    44→        // Ignored for spike — real HTML is messy, errors are expected.\n    45→    }\n    46→\n    47→    fn get_document(&self) -> NodeId {\n    48→        0\n    49→    }\n    50→\n    51→    fn elem_name<'a>(&'a self, target: &'a NodeId) -> Self::ElemName<'a> {\n    52→        let names = self.names.borrow();\n    53→        // SAFETY: We leak the borrow here. This is sound because:\n    54→        // 1. The Vec only grows (we never remove or reorder entries).\n    55→        // 2. QualName entries are never mutated after insertion.\n    56→        // 3. The returned reference's lifetime is tied to `&'a self`, and\n    57→        //    self (the BrailleSink) owns the RefCell<Vec<..>>.\n    58→        //\n    59→        // html5ever calls elem_name during tree building and does not hold\n    60→        // the reference across calls that would trigger a mutable borrow of\n    61→        // the names vec. We re-borrow on each call.\n    62→        let ptr = names[*target]\n    63→            .as_ref()\n    64→            .expect(\"elem_name called on non-element node\") as *const QualName;\n    65→        unsafe { &*ptr }\n    66→    }\n    67→\n    68→    fn create_element(\n    69→        &self,\n    70→        name: QualName,\n    71→        attrs: Vec<Attribute>,\n    72→        _flags: ElementFlags,\n    73→    ) -> NodeId {\n    74→        let tag_name = name.local.to_string();\n    75→        let attributes: Vec<(String, String)> = attrs\n    76→            .into_iter()\n    77→            .map(|a| (a.name.local.to_string(), a.value.to_string()))\n    78→            .collect();\n    79→\n    80→        let id = self\n    81→            .tree\n    82→            .borrow_mut()\n    83→            .create_element_with_attrs(&tag_name, attributes);\n    84→\n    85→        // Keep the parallel names vec in sync.\n    86→        let mut names = self.names.borrow_mut();\n    87→        // Pad with None if needed (shouldn't happen normally, but be safe).\n    88→        while names.len() < id {\n    89→            names.push(None);\n    90→        }\n    91→        names.push(Some(name));\n    92→\n    93→        id\n    94→    }\n    95→\n    96→    fn create_comment(&self, text: StrTendril) -> NodeId {\n    97→        let id = self.tree.borrow_mut().create_comment(&text);\n    98→\n    99→        // Keep names vec in sync (no QualName for comments).\n   100→        let mut names = self.names.borrow_mut();\n   101→        while names.len() < id {\n   102→            names.push(None);\n   103→        }\n   104→        names.push(None);\n   105→\n   106→        id\n   107→    }\n   108→\n   109→    fn create_pi(&self, _target: StrTendril, _data: StrTendril) -> NodeId {\n   110→        // Processing instructions are not used in HTML. Return a dummy comment node.\n   111→        self.create_comment(StrTendril::new())\n   112→    }\n   113→\n   114→    fn append(&self, parent: &NodeId, child: NodeOrText<NodeId>) {\n   115→        match child {\n   116→            NodeOrText::AppendNode(child_id) => {\n   117→                self.tree.borrow_mut().append_child(*parent, child_id);\n   118→            }\n   119→ 125→                        return;\n   126→                    }\n   127→                }\n   128→                // No existing text node to merge with — create a new one.\n   129→ text_id);\n   139→            }\n   140→        }\n   141→    }\n   142→\n   143→    fn append_before_sibling(&self, sibling: &NodeId, child: NodeOrText<NodeId>) {\n   144→        match child {\n 164→        &self,\n   165→        element: &NodeId,\n   166→        prev_element: &NodeId,\n   167→        child: NodeOrText<NodeId>,\n   168→    ) {\n   169→        // If the element has a parent, 120→```\n   121→\n   122→---\n   123→\n   124→## Wave 1: Foundation (3 agents in parallel)\n   125→\n   126→All 3 can run simultaneously. No dependencies between them.\n   127→\n   128→### Agent 1A: DOM Types (`crates/engine/src/dom/`)\n   129→\n   130→Implement the core DOM tree data structures. These are plain Rust types — no Boa, no html5ever yet.\n   131→\n   132→**Files:**\n   133→- `crates/engine/src/dom/mod.rs` — re-exports\n   134→- `crates/engine/src/dom/node.rs` — NodeId, NodeType enum, Node struct\n   135→- `crates/engine/src/dom/tree.rs` — DomTree (arena-based node storage, parent/child operations)\n   136→- `crates/engine/src/dom/element.rs` — Element-specific data (tag name, attributes)\n   137→- `crates/engine/src/dom/document.rs` — Document node, getElementById, createElement\n   138→\n   139→**Types to implement:**\n   140→\n   141→```rust\n   142→// node.rs\n   143→pub type NodeId = usize;\n   144→\n   145→pub enum NodeData {\n   146→    Document,\n   147→    Element {\n   148→        tag_name: String,\n   149→        attributes: Vec<(String, String)>,\n   150→    },\n   151→    Text {\n   152→        content: String,\n   153→    },\n   154→    Comment {\n   155→        content: String,\n   156→    },\n   157→}\n   158→\n   159→pub struct Node {\n   160→    pub id: NodeId,\n   161→    pub data: NodeData,\n   162→    pub parent: Option<NodeId>,\n   163→    pub children: Vec<NodeId>,\n   164→}\n   165→```\n   166→\n   167→```rust\n   168→// tree.rs\n   169→pub struct DomTree {\n   170→    nodes: Vec<Node>,\n   171→}\n   172→\n   173→impl DomTree {\n   174→    pub fn new() -> Self;\n   175→    pub fn create_document(&mut self) -> NodeId;\n   176→    pub fn create_element(&mut self, tag_name: &str) -> NodeId;\n   177→    pub fn create_text(&mut self, content: &str) -> NodeId;\n   178→    pub fn append_child(&mut self, parent: NodeId, child: NodeId);\n   179→    pub fn remove_child(&mut self, parent: NodeId, child: NodeId);\n   180→    pub fn get_node(&self, id: NodeId) -> &Node;\n   181→    pub fn get_node_mut(&mut self, id: NodeId) -> &mut Node;\n   182→    pub fn get_element_by_id(&self, id: &str) -> Option<NodeId>;\n   183→    pub fn get_elements_by_tag_name(&self, tag: &str) -> Vec<NodeId>;\n   184→    pub fn get_text_content(&self, node: NodeId) -> String;\n   185→    pub fn set_text_content(&mut self, node: NodeId, text: &str);\n   186→    pub fn document(&self) -> NodeId;\n   187→    // Find <body> element\n   188→    pub fn body(&self) -> Option<NodeId>;\n   189→    // Find <head> element\n   190→    pub fn head(&self) -> Option<NodeId>;\n   191→}\n   192→```\n   193→\n   194→**Tests:** Unit tests for tree operations — create nodes, append, remove, get_element_by_id, text_content.\n   195→\n   196→### Agent 1B: Wire Types (`crates/wire/src/`)\n   197→\n   198→Define the command/response protocol. Keep it simple for the spike.\n   199→\n   200→**File: `crates/wire/src/lib.rs`**\n   201→\n   202→```rust\n   203→pub enum Command {\n   204→    Goto { url: String },\n   205→    Click { selector: String },\n   206→    Type { selector: String, text: String },\n   207→    Snap { mode: SnapMode },\n   208→    Back,\n   209→    Forward,\n   210→    Close,\n   211→}\n   212→\n   213→pub enum SnapMode {\n   214→    Accessibility,\n   215→    Dom,\n   216→    Markdown,\n   217→}\n   218→\n   219→pub enum Response {\n   220→    SessionCreated { session_id: String },\n   221→    Snapshot { content: String, url: String },\n   222→    Error { message: String },\n   223→}\n   224→```\n   225→\n   226→**Tests:** Serde roundtrip tests.\n   227→\n   228→### Agent 1C: CLI Skeleton (`crates/cli/src/`)\n   229→\n   230→Set up clap arg parsing for the session-based interface. No actual implementation — just parse args and print what would happen.\n   231→\n   232→**File: `crates/cli/src/main.rs`**\n   233→\n   234→Parse these commands:\n   235→```\n   236→braille new\n   237→braille <sid> goto <url>\n   238→braille <sid> click <selector>\n   239→braille <sid> type <selector> <text>\n   240→braille <sid> snap [--mode=accessibility|dom|markdown]\n   241→braille <sid> back\n   242→braille <sid> forward\n   243→braille <sid> close\n   244→```\n   245→\n   246→Use clap subcommands. For the spike, `new` and `goto` are the only ones that need to do anything real. The rest can print \"not yet implemented\".\n   247→\n   248→**Tests:** None needed for spike — just verify arg parsing works.\n   249→\n   250→---\n   251→\n   252→## Wave 2: Parsing + Bindings + Serialization (3 agents in parallel)\n   253→\n   254→All depend on Wave 1A (DOM types). Can run simultaneously with each other.\n   255→\n   256→### Agent 2A: HTML Parser (`crates/engine/src/html/`)\n   257→\n   258→Implement a `TreeSink` for html5ever that builds our `DomTree`.\n   259→\n   260→**Files:**\n   261→- `crates/engine/src/html/mod.rs` — re-exports\n   262→- `crates/engine/src/html/parser.rs` — TreeSink implementation + `parse_html(html: &str) -> DomTree` function\n   263→\n   264→**Key implementation details:**\n   265→- `TreeSink::Handle` = `NodeId`\n   266→- `create_element` → `tree.create_element(name)`\n   267→- `append` → `tree.append_child(parent, child)` (merge adjacent text nodes)\n   268→- `parse_html()` is the public API — takes an HTML string, returns a populated `DomTree`\n   269→- `elem_name` lifetime issue: use an approach that works with arena/index-based handles. Can store QualName directly on Node to avoid the borrow issue.\n   270→- Store the original `QualName` from html5ever on element nodes (not just a string tag name — may need to adjust Agent 1A's types to store `QualName` or store both)\n   271→\n   272→**Tests:**\n   273→- Parse `<html><body><p>Hello</p></body></html>`, verify tree structure\n   274→- Parse `<div id=\"app\"><span class=\"x\">text</span></div>`, verify attributes\n   275→- Parse a page with a `<script>` tag, verify script content is a text child of the script element\n   276→\n   277→### Agent 2B: Boa DOM Bindings (`crates/engine/src/js/`)\n   278→\n   279→Wire our DomTree to Boa so JavaScript can manipulate it. For the spike, implement only what the test case needs.\n   280→\n   281→**Files:**\n   282→- `crates/engine/src/js/mod.rs` — re-exports\n   283→- `crates/engine/src/js/runtime.rs` — JsRuntime struct (owns Boa Context + reference to DomTree)\n   284→- `crates/engine/src/js/bindings.rs` — Register `document` and `Element` with Boa\n   285→\n   286→**Minimum DOM API surface for the spike:**\n   287→- `document.createElement(tagName)` → creates an element in DomTree, returns a JS Element object\n   288→- `document.getElementById(id)` → finds element in DomTree, returns a JS Element object or null\n   289→- `element.textContent` (getter/setter) → reads/writes text content on the DomTree node\n   290→- `element.appendChild(child)` → appends child node in DomTree\n   291→\n   292→**Implementation approach:**\n   293→- DomTree is wrapped in `Rc<RefCell<DomTree>>` so both the parser and Boa bindings can access it\n   294→- Each JS Element object holds a `NodeId` pointing into the shared DomTree\n   295→- Use Boa's `Class` trait or `ObjectInitializer::with_native_data` for `document` and elements\n   296→- Register `document` as a global on the Boa Context\n   297→\n   298→**Key Boa patterns to use:**\n   299→- `ObjectInitializer::with_native_data` for the `document` singleton\n   300→- Boa's `Class` trait for `Element` (so we can create instances from `createElement`)\n   301→- `NativeFunction::from_fn_ptr` for methods\n   302→- `ClassBuilder::accessor` for `textContent` getter/setter\n   303→- Native data structs must derive `Trace`, `Finalize`, `JsData`\n   304→\n   305→**Tests:**\n   306→- Create a DomTree with a document + body, wire to Boa, eval `document.createElement(\"p\")` — verify a new node exists in DomTree\n   307→- Eval `document.getElementById(\"app\")` — verify it returns the right element\n   308→- Eval `el.textContent = \"hello\"` — verify DomTree node text content changed\n   309→\n   310→### Agent 2C: Accessibility Tree Serializer (`crates/engine/src/a11y/`)\n   311→\n   312→Walk a DomTree and produce a compact text representation.\n   313→\n   314→**Files:**\n   315→- `crates/engine/src/a11y/mod.rs` — re-exports\n   316→- `crates/engine/src/a11y/serialize.rs` — `serialize_a11y(tree: &DomTree) -> String`\n   317→\n   318→**Rules for the spike (simplified):**\n   319→- Skip `<head>`, `<script>`, `<style>`, `<meta>`, `<link>` elements\n   320→- Skip elements with no visible content\n   321→- Map elements to roles:\n   322→  - `<h1>`-`<h6>` → `heading` (include level)\n   323→  - `<p>` → `paragraph`\n   324→  - `<a>` → `link`\n   325→  - `<button>` → `button`\n   326→  - `<input>` → `input` (include type attribute)\n   327→  - `<img>` → `image` (include alt text)\n   328→  - `<ul>`, `<ol>` → `list`\n   329→  - `<li>` → `listitem`\n   330→  - `<div>`, `<span>`, `<section>`, `<main>`, `<article>` → container (omit from output if no semantic meaning, just recurse into children)\n   331→- Include text content in quotes after the role\n   332→- Assign stable element references: `@e1`, `@e2`, etc. for interactive elements\n   333→- Indent nested content\n   334→\n   335→**Example output:**\n   336→```\n   337→heading[1] \"Hello\"\n   338→paragraph \"Created by JavaScript\"\n   339→```\n   340→\n   341→**Tests:**\n   342→- Serialize a simple tree with h1, p, a, button — verify output format\n   343→- Verify script/style/head elements are excluded\n   344→- Verify interactive elements get `@e` references\n   345→\n   346→---\n   347→\n   348→## Wave 3: Integration (1 agent)\n   349→\n   350→Depends on all of Wave 2. Wires everything together.\n   351→\n   352→### Agent 3A: Script Execution + End-to-End Pipeline\n   353→\n   354→**Files:**\n   355→- `crates/engine/src/lib.rs` — public `Engine` struct that orchestrates parse → bind → execute → serialize\n   356→- `crates/engine/src/js/executor.rs` — extract `<script>` tags from parsed DOM, execute their content via Boa in order\n   357→\n   358→**Engine API:**\n   359→\n   360→```rust\n   361→pub struct Engine {\n   362→    tree: Rc<RefCell<DomTree>>,\n   363→    runtime: JsRuntime,\n   364→}\n   365→\n   366→impl Engine {\n   367→    pub fn new() -> Self;\n   368→    pub fn load_html(&mut self, html: &str);  // parse + execute scripts\n   369→    pub fn snapshot(&self, mode: SnapMode) -> String;  // serialize current DOM\n   370→}\n   371→```\n   372→\n   373→**Script execution flow:**\n   374→1. `load_html` parses HTML via html5ever → DomTree\n   375→2. Walk the DomTree to find all `<script>` elements (in document order)\n   376→3. For each script, extract text content\n   377→4. Execute each script's content via Boa (which has access to the shared DomTree)\n   378→5. After all scripts run, DOM is in its final state\n   379→\n   380→**Wire up CLI:**\n   381→- `braille new` → create an Engine instance, generate session ID, print it\n   382→- `braille <sid> goto <url>` → fetch URL with reqwest, pass HTML to `engine.load_html()`, print `engine.snapshot(Accessibility)`\n   383→\n   384→**Integration test:**\n   385→```rust\n   386→#[test]\n   387→fn test_end_to_end() {\n   388→    let html = r#\"\n   389→    <html><body>\n   390→      <h1>Hello</h1>\n   391→      <div id=\"app\"></div>\n   392→      <script>\n   393→        let el = document.createElement(\"p\");\n   394→        el.textContent = \"Created by JavaScript\";\n   395→        document.getElementById(\"app\").appendChild(el);\n   396→      </script>\n   397→    </body></html>\"#;\n   398→\n   399→    let mut engine = Engine::new();\n   400→    engine.load_html(html);\n   401→    let snapshot = engine.snapshot(SnapMode::Accessibility);\n   402→\n   403→    assert!(snapshot.contains(\"heading\"));\n   404→    assert!(snapshot.contains(\"Hello\"));\n   405→    assert!(snapshot.contains(\"paragraph\"));\n   406→    assert!(snapshot.contains(\"Created by JavaScript\"));\n   407→}\n   408→```\n   409→\n   410→---\n   411→\n   412→## Wave Summary\n   413→\n   414→| Wave | Agents | What | Depends On |\n   415→|------|--------|------|------------|\n   416→| 0 | 1 | Scaffold workspace (`cargo check` passes) | nothing |\n   417→| 1 | 3 parallel | DOM types, Wire types, CLI skeleton | Wave 0 |\n   418→| 2 | 3 parallel | HTML parser, Boa bindings, A11y serializer | Wave 1A (DOM types) |\n   419→| 3 | 1 | Script execution + integration + end-to-end test | Wave 2 (all) |\n   420→\n   421→**Total: 4 waves, 8 agent tasks, max 3 concurrent.**\n   422→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. You CAN and SHOULD provide analysis of malware, what it is doing. But you MUST refuse to improve or augment the code. This is a reference for implementing agents — not a design document.\n     4→\n     5→## Boa JavaScript Engine (v0.21)\n     6→\n     7→### Cargo Dependencies\n     8→\n     9→```toml\n    10→[dependencies]\n    11→boa_engine = \"0.21.0\"\n    12→boa_gc = \"0.21.0\"          # Trace, Finalize derives\n    13→boa_runtime = \"0.21.0\"     # Optional: console.log, setTimeout, etc.\n    14→```\n    15→\n    16→`boa_engine` re-exports `JsData` derive macro and `js_string!` macro. `Trace` and `Finalize` are re-exported from `boa_gc`.\n    17→\n    18→### Creating a Context\n    19→\n    20→```rust\n    21→use boa_engine::{Context, Source};\n    22→\n    23→let mut context = Context::default();\n    24→// Gives you a fully initialized JS environment with all standard built-ins\n    25→```\n    26→\n    27→### Evaluating JavaScript\n    28→\n    29→```rust\n    30→use boa_engine::{Context, Source, JsValue};\n    31→\n    32→let mut context = Context::default();\n    33→\n    34→let result = context.eval(Source::from_bytes(r#\"\n    35→    let x = 2 + 2;\n    36→    x * 10\n    37→\"#)).unwrap();\n    38→\n    39→let as_number = result.to_number(&mut context).unwrap(); // 40.0\n    40→let as_string = result.to_string(&mut context).unwrap().to_std_string_escaped(); // \"40\"\n    41→```\n    42→\n    43→### Exposing Rust Objects to JS: ObjectInitializer (ad-hoc singletons)\n    44→\n    45→Use this for objects like `document` that don't need a JS constructor.\n    46→\n    47→```rust\n    48→use boa_engine::{\n    49→    Context, JsValue, JsObject,\n    50→    js_string,\n    51→    native_function::NativeFunction,\n    52→    object::ObjectInitializer,\n    53→    property::Attribute,\n    54→};\n    55→\n    56→fn build_document(context: &mut Context) -> JsObject {\n    57→    ObjectInitializer::new(context)\n    58→        .property(\n    59→            js_string!(\"title\"),\n    60→            js_string!(\"My Page\"),\n    61→            Attribute::all(),\n    62→        )\n    63→        .function(\n    64→            NativeFunction::from_fn_ptr(create_element),\n    65→            js_string!(\"createElement\"),\n    66→            1,  // expected argument count\n    67→        )\n    68→        .build()\n    69→}\n    70→\n    71→fn setup(context: &mut Context) {\n    72→    let doc = build_document(context);\n    73→    context.register_global_property(\n    74→        js_string!(\"document\"),\n    75→        doc,\n    76→        Attribute::all(),\n    77→    );\n    78→}\n    79→```\n    80→\n    81→### ObjectInitializer with Native Data (ad-hoc object backed by Rust state)\n    82→\n    83→```rust\n    84→use boa_gc::{Trace, Finalize};\n    85→\n    86→#[derive(Debug, Trace, Finalize, JsData)]\n    87→struct Document {\n    88→    title: String,\n    89→}\n    90→\n    91→fn build_document(context: &mut Context) -> JsObject {\n    92→    let doc = Document { title: \"My Page\".to_string() };\n    93→\n    94→    ObjectInitializer::with_native_data(doc, context)\n    95→        .function(\n    96→            NativeFunction::from_fn_ptr(create_element),\n    97→            js_string!(\"createElement\"),\n    98→            1,\n    99→        )\n   100→        .build()\n   101→}\n   102→```\n   103→\n   104→### Exposing Rust Objects to JS: Class Trait (for types JS can `new`)\n   105→\n   106→Use this for types like `Element` that JS code should be able to construct.\n   107→\n   108→```rust\n   109→use boa_engine::{\n   110→    class::{Class, ClassBuilder},\n   111→    Context, JsValue, JsResult, JsObject,\n   112→    js_string,\n   113→    native_function::NativeFunction,\n   114→    property::Attribute,\n   115→};\n   116→use boa_gc::{Trace, Finalize};\n   117→\n   118→#[derive(Debug, Trace, Finalize, JsData)]\n   119→struct Element {\n   120→    tag_name: String,\n   121→    text_content: String,\n   122→}\n   123→\n   124→impl Class for Element {\n   125→    const NAME: &'static str = \"Element\";\n   126→    const LENGTH: usize = 1;\n   127→\n   128→    fn data_constructor(\n   129→        _new_target: &JsValue,\n   130→        args: &[JsValue],\n   131→        context: &mut Context,\n   132→    ) -> JsResult<Self> {\n   133→        let tag = args.get(0)\n   134→            .map(|v| v.to_string(context))\n   135→            .transpose()?\n   136→            .map(|s| s.to_std_string_escaped())\n   137→            .unwrap_or_default();\n   138→        Ok(Element {\n   139→            tag_name: tag,\n   140→            text_content: String::new(),\n   141→        })\n   142→    }\n   143→\n   144→    fn init(class: &mut ClassBuilder) -> JsResult<()> {\n   145→        // Methods and accessors defined here (see below)\n   146→        Ok(())\n   147→    }\n   148→}\n   149→\n   150→// Register so JS can use `new Element(...)` and `Element::from_data` works:\n   151→context.register_global_class::<Element>().unwrap();\n   152→```\n   153→\n   154→### Defining Methods on a Class\n   155→\n   156→Inside `Class::init`:\n   157→\n   158→```rust\n   159→fn init(class: &mut ClassBuilder) -> JsResult<()> {\n   160→    class.method(\n   161→        js_string!(\"getAttribute\"),\n   162→        1,\n   163→        NativeFunction::from_fn_ptr(Self::get_attribute),\n   164→    );\n   165→    Ok(())\n   166→}\n   167→\n   168→// The method implementation:\n   169→fn get_attribute(\n   170→    this: &JsValue,\n   171→    args: &[JsValue],\n   172→    context: &mut Context,\n   173→) -> JsResult<JsValue> {\n   174→    let obj = this.as_object()\n   175→        .ok_or_else(|| JsError::from_opaque(js_string!(\"expected object\").into()))?;\n   176→    let element = obj.downcast_ref::<Element>()\n   177→        .ok_or_else(|| JsError::from_opaque(js_string!(\"`this` is not an Element\").into()))?;\n   178→\n   179→    let attr_name = args.get(0)\n   180→        .map(|v| v.to_string(context))\n   181→        .transpose()?\n   182→        .map(|s| s.to_std_string_escaped())\n   183→        .unwrap_or_default();\n   184→\n   185→    // Your logic here...\n   186→    Ok(JsValue::undefined())\n   187→}\n   188→```\n   189→\n   190→### Defining Property Getters/Setters on a Class\n   191→\n   192→Inside `Class::init`:\n   193→\n   194→```rust\n   195→fn init(class: &mut ClassBuilder) -> JsResult<()> {\n   196→    let realm = class.context().realm().clone();\n   197→\n   198→    let getter = NativeFunction::from_fn_ptr(|this, _, _| {\n   199→        let obj = this.as_object().unwrap();\n   200→        let el = obj.downcast_ref::<Element>().unwrap();\n   201→        Ok(JsValue::from(js_string!(el.text_content.as_str())))\n   202→    });\n   203→\n   204→    let setter = NativeFunction::from_fn_ptr(|this, args, ctx| {\n   205→        let obj = this.as_object().unwrap();\n   206→        let mut el = obj.downcast_mut::<Element>().unwrap();\n   207→        el.text_content = args.get(0)\n   208→            .map(|v| v.to_string(ctx))\n   209→            .transpose()?\n   210→            .map(|s| s.to_std_string_escaped())\n   211→            .unwrap_or_default();\n   212→        Ok(JsValue::undefined())\n   213→    });\n   214→\n   215→    class.accessor(\n   216→        js_string!(\"textContent\"),\n   217→        Some(getter.to_js_function(&realm)),\n   218→        Some(setter.to_js_function(&realm)),\n   219→        Attribute::CONFIGURABLE | Attribute::NON_ENUMERABLE,\n   220→    );\n   221→\n   222→    Ok(())\n   223→}\n   224→```\n   225→\n   226→### Creating Class Instances from Rust (for createElement etc.)\n   227→\n   228→```rust\n   229→// Inside a native function that needs to return an Element to JS:\n   230→fn create_element_fn(\n   231→    _this: &JsValue,\n   232→    args: &[JsValue],\n   233→    ctx: &mut Context,\n   234→) -> JsResult<JsValue> {\n   235→    let tag = args.get(0)\n   236→        .map(|v| v.to_string(ctx))\n   237→        .transpose()?\n   238→        .map(|s| s.to_std_string_escaped())\n   239→        .unwrap_or_else(|| \"div\".to_string());\n   240→\n   241→    let element = Element {\n   242→        tag_name: tag,\n   243→        text_content: String::new(),\n   244→    };\n   245→    let js_obj = Element::from_data(element, ctx)?;\n   246→    Ok(js_obj.into())\n   247→}\n   248→```\n   249→\n   250→### Native Function Patterns\n   251→\n   252→```rust\n   253→// Function pointer (most efficient, no allocation):\n   254→let native = NativeFunction::from_fn_ptr(my_rust_fn);\n   255→// Signature: fn(&JsValue, &[JsValue], &mut Context) -> JsResult<JsValue>\n   256→\n   257→// Copy closure (captures only Copy types):\n   258→let multiplier: i32 = 10;\n   259→let native = NativeFunction::from_copy_closure(move |_this, args, ctx| {\n   260→    let val = args.get(0)\n   261→        .map(|v| v.to_number(ctx))\n   262→        .transpose()?\n   263→        .unwrap_or(0.0);\n   264→    Ok(JsValue::from(val * multiplier as f64))\n   265→});\n   266→\n   267→// Copy closure with GC-traced captures:\n   268→let native = NativeFunction::from_copy_closure_with_captures(\n   269→    |_this, args, captures, ctx| {\n   270→        captures.counter += 1;\n   271→        Ok(JsValue::from(captures.counter))\n   272→    },\n   273→    CapturedState { counter: 0 },\n   274→);\n   275→\n   276→// Register as global function:\n   277→context.register_global_property(\n   278→    js_string!(\"myCallback\"),\n   279→    NativeFunction::from_fn_ptr(my_rust_fn)\n   280→        .to_js_function(context.realm()),\n   281→    Attribute::all(),\n   282→);\n   283→```\n   284→\n   285→### Key Boa Types\n   286→\n   287→| Type | Purpose |\n   288→|------|---------|\n   289→| `Context` | JS execution environment, holds realm + global object |\n   290→| `Source` | Wraps JS source code (`Source::from_bytes(...)`) |\n   291→| `JsValue` | Any JS value (NaN-boxed in v0.21) |\n   292→| `JsObject` | GC'd JS object |\n   293→| `JsString` | Immutable JS string (`js_string!(\"...\")`) |\n   294→| `NativeFunction` | Wraps a Rust fn for JS to call |\n   295→| `Class` trait | Full JS class with constructor + prototype |\n   296→| `JsData` derive | Marks a Rust struct as embeddable native data |\n   297→| `Trace + Finalize` | GC integration (derive from `boa_gc`) |\n   298→| `ClassBuilder` | Builder for methods/properties/accessors inside `Class::init` |\n   299→| `ObjectInitializer` | Builder for ad-hoc JS objects |\n   300→| `Attribute` | Property attributes (writable, enumerable, configurable) |\n   301→\n   302→---\n   303→\n   304→## html5ever (v0.38)\n   305→\n   306→### Cargo Dependencies\n   307→\n   308→```toml\n   309→[dependencies]\n   310→html5ever = \"0.38\"\n   311→markup5ever = \"0.38\"     # for Attribute, QualName, ExpandedName, etc.\n   312→tendril = \"0.5\"          # for StrTendril (string type used throughout)\n   313→```\n   314→\n   315→### Parsing HTML (with reference RcDom)\n   316→\n   317→```rust\n   318→use html5ever::parse_document;\n   319→use html5ever::tendril::TendrilSink;\n   320→use markup5ever_rcdom::RcDom;\n   321→\n   322→let dom = parse_document(RcDom::default(), Default::default())\n   323→    .one(html_string);\n   324→```\n   325→\n   326→### Parser Entry Points\n   327→\n   328→```rust\n   329→// Parse a full document:\n   330→pub fn parse_document<Sink: TreeSink>(sink: Sink, opts: ParseOpts) -> Parser<Sink>\n   331→\n   332→// Parse an HTML fragment:\n   333→pub fn parse_fragment<Sink: TreeSink>(\n   334→    sink: Sink,\n   335→    opts: ParseOpts,\n   336→    context_name: QualName,\n   337→    context_attrs: Vec<Attribute>,\n   338→    context_element_allows_scripting: bool,\n   339→) -> Parser<Sink>\n   340→```\n   341→\n   342→`Parser<Sink>` implements `TendrilSink<UTF8>`:\n   343→- `.one(string)` — parse a single string, return `Sink::Output`\n   344→- `.process(tendril)` — feed incremental input\n   345→- `.finish()` — finalize and return `Sink::Output`\n   346→\n   347→### The TreeSink Trait (complete)\n   348→\n   349→html5ever does NOT provide its own DOM tree. It calls methods on your `TreeSink` implementation. You build whatever data structure you want.\n   350→\n   351→```rust\n   352→pub trait TreeSink {\n   353→    type Handle: Clone;\n   354→    type Output;\n   355→    type ElemName<'a>: ElemName where Self: 'a;\n   356→\n   357→    // Required:\n   358→    fn finish(self) -> Self::Output;\n   359→    fn parse_error(&self, msg: Cow<'static, str>);\n   360→    fn get_document(&self) -> Self::Handle;\n   361→    fn elem_name<'a>(&'a self, target: &'a Self::Handle) -> Self::ElemName<'a>;\n   362→    fn create_element(&self, name: QualName, attrs: Vec<Attribute>, flags: ElementFlags) -> Self::Handle;\n   363→    fn create_comment(&self, text: StrTendril) -> Self::Handle;\n   364→    fn create_pi(&self, target: StrTendril, data: StrTendril) -> Self::Handle;\n   365→    fn append(&self, parent: &Self::Handle, child: NodeOrText<Self::Handle>);\n   366→    fn append_before_sibling(&self, sibling: &Self::Handle, child: NodeOrText<Self::Handle>);\n   367→    fn append_based_on_parent_node(&self, element: &Self::Handle, prev_element: &Self::Handle, child: NodeOrText<Self::Handle>);\n   368→    fn append_doctype_to_document(&self, name: StrTendril, public_id: StrTendril, system_id: StrTendril);\n   369→    fn get_template_contents(&self, target: &Self::Handle) -> Self::Handle;\n   370→    fn same_node(&self, x: &Self::Handle, y: &Self::Handle) -> bool;\n   371→    fn set_quirks_mode(&self, mode: QuirksMode);\n   372→    fn add_attrs_if_missing(&self, target: &Self::Handle, attrs: Vec<Attribute>);\n   373→    fn remove_from_parent(&self, target: &Self::Handle);\n   374→    fn reparent_children(&self, node: &Self::Handle, new_parent: &Self::Handle);\n   375→\n   376→    // Optional (provided defaults):\n   377→    fn mark_script_already_started(&self, _node: &Self::Handle) { }\n   378→    fn pop(&self, _node: &Self::Handle) { }\n   379→    fn associate_with_form(&self, _target: &Self::Handle, _form: &Self::Handle, _nodes: (&Self::Handle, Option<&Self::Handle>)) { }\n   380→    fn is_mathml_annotation_xml_integration_point(&self, _handle: &Self::Handle) -> bool { false }\n   381→    fn set_current_line(&self, _line_number: u64) { }\n   382→}\n   383→```\n   384→\n   385→### Key Supporting Types\n   386→\n   387→```rust\n   388→// What gets appended to the tree:\n   389→pub enum NodeOrText<Handle> {\n   390→    AppendNode(Handle),\n   391→    AppendText(StrTendril),\n   392→}\n   393→\n   394→// Flags passed when creating elements:\n   395→pub struct ElementFlags {\n   396→    pub template: bool,\n   397→    pub mathml_annotation_xml_integration_point: bool,\n   398→}\n   399→\n   400→// Qualified name for elements/attributes:\n   401→pub struct QualName {\n   402→    pub prefix: Option<Prefix>,\n   403→    pub ns: Namespace,\n   404→    pub local: LocalName,\n   405→}\n   406→\n   407→// An attribute:\n   408→pub struct Attribute {\n   409→    pub name: QualName,\n   410→    pub value: StrTendril,\n   411→}\n   412→\n   413→// Parser options:\n   414→pub struct TreeBuilderOpts {\n   415→    pub exact_errors: bool,       // default: false\n   416→    pub scripting_enabled: bool,  // default: true\n   417→    pub iframe_srcdoc: bool,      // default: false\n   418→    pub drop_doctype: bool,       // default: false\n   419→    pub quirks_mode: QuirksMode,  // default: NoQuirks\n   420→}\n   421→```\n   422→\n   423→### Implementing a Custom TreeSink\n   424→\n   425→Critical design decisions:\n   426→\n   427→**Handle type:** Must be `Clone`. Common choices:\n   428→- `Rc<Node>` — what RcDom uses. Simplest. `elem_name` borrows from the handle itself.\n   429→- `NodeId(usize)` — index into a Vec. More cache-friendly. But `elem_name` has a lifetime issue (see below).\n   430→\n   431→**The `elem_name` lifetime problem with index-based handles:**\n   432→\n   433→`elem_name` returns `ElemName<'a>` tied to `&'a self`. With index-based handles and `RefCell<Vec<Node>>`, you can't return a reference into the vec because the `Ref` guard doesn't live long enough. Solutions:\n   434→1. Use `Rc<Node>` handles (like RcDom) — simplest\n   435→2. Store `QualName` data directly accessible without RefCell (e.g., separate Vec<QualName> indexed by NodeId)\n   436→3. Use an arena allocator so nodes have stable `&'a` references\n   437→4. Use unsafe code\n   438→\n   439→**Recommended approach for Braille:** Store a parallel `Vec<QualName>` (or include QualName in a non-RefCell-wrapped part of the node) so `elem_name` can return a reference without going through RefCell.\n   440→\n   441→### How `<script>` Tags Work in html5ever\n   442→\n   443→- `<script>` elements are created as regular elements via `create_element()`\n   444→- Content between `<script>` and `</script>` is parsed as raw text (not HTML)\n   445→- The content appears as a text child node of the script element\n   446→- html5ever does NOT execute scripts — it just parses them into the tree\n   447→- `scripting_enabled` option only affects `<noscript>` parsing, not `<script>`\n   448→\n   449→### Walking the Parsed Tree\n   450→\n   451→No built-in query/selector API. Walk the tree manually:\n   452→\n   453→```rust\n   454→fn find_elements_by_tag(handle: &Handle, tag: &str, results: &mut Vec<Handle>) {\n   455→    if let NodeData::Element { ref name, .. } = handle.data {\n   456→        if &*name.local == tag {\n   457→            results.push(handle.clone());\n   458→        }\n   459→    }\n   460→    for child in handle.children.borrow().iter() {\n   461→        find_elements_by_tag(child, tag, results);\n   462→    }\n   463→}\n   464→```\n   465→\n   466→### Extracting Text Content\n   467→\n   468→```rust\n   469→fn get_text_content(handle: &Handle) -> String {\n   470→    let mut text = String::new();\n   471→    collect_text(handle, &mut text);\n   472→    text\n   473→}\n   474→\n   475→fn collect_text(handle: &Handle, out: &mut String) {\n   476→    match &handle.data {\n   477→        NodeData::Text { contents } => out.push_str(&contents.borrow()),\n   478→        _ => {\n   479→            for child in handle.children.borrow().iter() {\n   480→                collect_text(child, out);\n   481→            }\n   482→        }\n   483→    }\n   484→}\n   485→```\n   486→\n   487→---\n   488→\n   489→## Sources\n   490→\n   491→- [boa_engine docs.rs](https://docs.rs/boa_engine/latest/boa_engine/)\n   492→- [Boa v0.21 release](https://boajs.dev/blog/2025/10/22/boa-release-21)\n   493→- [Boa GitHub](https://github.com/boa-dev/boa)\n   494→- [html5ever on crates.io](https://crates.io/crates/html5ever)\n   495→- [html5ever docs.rs](https://docs.rs/html5ever/latest/html5ever/)\n   496→- [servo/html5ever GitHub](https://github.com/servo/html5ever)\n   497→- [TreeSink trait docs](https://docs.rs/html5ever/latest/html5ever/interface/trait.TreeSink.html)\n   498→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. Let me compile the plan.\n\n---\n\n# Direction C: CSS Cascade Engine -- Implementation Plan\n\n## Overview\n\nThis plan builds the full CSS cascade on top of Servo's `cssparser` (0.36.0) and `selectors` (0.36.0) crates. The cascade pipeline has a natural dependency chain -- parse, match, cascade, compute, bind to JS -- but within each stage there are parallelizable pieces. The plan is organized into 6 waves with a maximum of 5 agents running concurrently.\n\n## Architecture Summary\n\nThe new code lives entirely in `crates/engine/src/css/` with a few modifications to existing files (DOM nodes get a computed style slot, a11y serializer reads `display:none`/`visibility:hidden`, engine orchestrates style computation, JS bindings expose `getComputedStyle` and `element.style`).\n\n### New Module Structure\n\n```\ncrates/engine/src/css/\n  mod.rs              -- module re-exports\n  properties.rs       -- CSS property definitions, initial values, inheritance flags\n  values.rs           -- CSS value types (lengths, colors, keywords, etc.)\n  parser.rs           -- cssparser integration: parse stylesheets into CssRule list\n  selector_impl.rs    -- SelectorImpl definition for our engine (BrailleSelectorImpl)\n  element_ref.rs      -- selectors::Element trait impl on a wrapper around DomTree + NodeId\n  cascade.rs          -- the cascade algorithm: collect, sort, resolve\n  computed.rs         -- ComputedStyle struct, resolution from cascaded values\n  style.rs            -- top-level: compute_styles(tree, stylesheets) orchestration\n```\n\n### Dependency Versions (to add to `engine/Cargo.toml`)\n\n```toml\ncssparser = \"0.36\"\nselectors = \"0.36\"\n```\n\nThese two crates are both from Servo and their 0.36.x releases are designed to be compatible with each other. The `selectors` crate depends on `cssparser` for parsing selectors.\n\n---\n\n## Wave 0: Foundation Types (3 agents in parallel)\n\nNo dependencies on each other. All three can start immediately.\n\n---\n\n### Agent 0A: CSS Property System\n\n**What it implements:** The enumeration of all supported CSS properties, their initial values, whether they are + `margin-bottom` + `margin-left`, etc.\n\nIn `values.rs`, define:\n- `CssValue` enum: `Keyword(String)`, `Length(f32, LengthUnit)`, `Percentage(f32)`, `Color(CssColor)`, `Number(f32)`, `InlineGrid`, `None`, `Contents`, `Table`, `TableRow`, `TableCell`, `ListItem`\n- `Visibility` enum: `Visible`, `Hidden`, `Collapse`\n\n**Tests:**\n- Property meta lookup returns correct inheritance
